<script>
    window.addEventListener('load', function () {
        const announcementBar = document.getElementById('announcement-bar');
        const messages = [
            document.getElementById('message1'),
            document.getElementById('message2'),
            document.getElementById('message3'),
        ];

        // Retrieve the last shown message index from localStorage
        let currentIndex = parseInt(localStorage.getItem('currentMessageIndex') || '0', 10);

        // Hide all messages initially
        messages.forEach((message) => {
            message.style.display = 'none';
        });

        // Show the current message
        messages[currentIndex].style.display = 'flex';

        // Show the announcement bar
        setTimeout(() => {
            announcementBar.style.display = 'flex';
            document.body.classList.add('with-announcement');
        }, 10000); // 10-second delay

        // Update the index for the next page load
        currentIndex = (currentIndex + 1) % messages.length;
        localStorage.setItem('currentMessageIndex', currentIndex);

        // Close button functionality
        document.getElementById('close-announcement').addEventListener('click', function () {
            announcementBar.style.display = 'none';
            document.body.classList.remove('with-announcement');
        });
    });
</script>

{"@context":"https:\/\/schema.org\/","@type":"NewsArticle","@id":"https:\/\/cyble.com\/blog\/lummac2-stealer-a-potent-threat-to-crypto-users\/#newsarticle","url":"https:\/\/cyble.com\/blog\/lummac2-stealer-a-potent-threat-to-crypto-users\/","headline":"Cyble - LummaC2 Stealer: A Potent Threat to Crypto Users","mainEntityOfPage":"https:\/\/cyble.com\/blog\/lummac2-stealer-a-potent-threat-to-crypto-users\/","datePublished":"2023-01-06T08:42:39-05:00","dateModified":"2024-10-21T10:45:51-04:00","description":"CRIL analyzes the latest version of LummaC2 Stealer , targeting crypto users via stealing their crypto wallet and 2FA extensions.","articleSection":"Cryptominer","articleBody":"New Stealer Targeting Crypto Wallets and 2FA Extensions of Various Browsers        During a threat-hunting exercise, Cyble Research and Intelligence Labs (CRIL) discovered a post on the cybercrime forum about an information stealer targeting both Chromium and Mozilla-based browsers. This stealer was named LummaC2 Stealer, which targets crypto wallets, extensions, and two-factor authentication (2FA) and steals sensitive information from the victim's machine.    The figure below shows the dark web post by the Threat Actors.    Figure 1 - Dark Web Post for LummaC2 Stealer        The post also mentioned the link to LummaC2 Stealer's seller website, which is written in Russian. The website also offers various purchasing options for potential Threat Actors(TAs), with prices ranging from $250 to $20000 depending on the plan.    The image below shows the website where the stealer is available for sale.    Figure 2 - LummaC2 Stealer Sellers Website        In addition, Threat Actors (TAs) behind the LummaC2 Stealer have created two Telegram channels in Russian: one for sharing information about the stealer and one for reporting bugs in the malware.    Figure 3 - Telegram Post by the Threat Actors        The researchers at CRIL found two active Command and Control servers connected to the LummaC2 Stealer.    The figure below illustrates the IP addresses of these servers, one located in Bulgaria and the other in Germany.    Figure 4 - LummaC2 Stealer C&amp;C IPs        The figure below shows the login page of the LummaC2 Stealer's Command and Control (C&amp;C) server.    Figure 5 - LummaC2 C&amp;C panel Login Page        Technical Details        The LummaC2 Stealer is a 32-bit GUI type executable with sha256 d932ee10f02ea5bb60ed867d9687a906f1b8472f01fc5543b06f9ab22059b264.    The figure below shows the additional file details of the LummaC2 stealer executable.    Figure 6 - File Details of LummaC2 Stealer        Detection Evasion:        The stealer has many Obfuscated strings that are being covered by a random string, \"edx765\", to evade detection. Upon execution, the stealer passes the obfuscated string to a function that strips the random string and delivers the original string.    The figure below shows the routine for string manipulation.    Figure 7 - Assembly Code to Replace the edx765 String        Collects System Information:        After getting the required strings, the malware resolves the APIs. It starts extracting multiple pieces of information from the system, including LummaC2 Build, Lumma ID, Hardware ID, Screen Resolution, System Language, CPU Name, and Physical Memory. The malware stores this information in the memory under the name system.txt.    The below figure shows the code snippet of malware for collecting system information.    Figure 8&nbsp;- System Information Extracted by the Stealer        File Grabber:        The stealer now enumerates the %userProfile% directory and grabs .txt files from the Victims machine. These grabbed files are stored in the memory under the name \"Important Files\/Profile\" for exfiltration.    Wallets:        The stealer also targets crypto wallets such as Binance, Electrum, and Ethereum and collects sensitive information from the victim's machine. The below figure shows the code snippet of stealers targeting crypto wallets.    Figure 9&nbsp;- The Stealer Targeting Wallets        After collecting the victim's wallet and system details, the stealer sends this information to its C&amp;C server, as shown below.    Figure 10 &nbsp;- Initial C&amp;C Communication of the Stealer        Browsers:        After sending the stolen information, the stealer checks for the following browsers installed on the system: Chrome, Chromium, Edge, Kometa, Vivaldi, Brave, Opera Stable, Opera GX Stable, Opera Neon, and Mozilla Firefox and steals sensitive information from the browsers.    The figure below shows the code to check the browsers.    Figure 11&nbsp;- Stealer Checking for the Browsers in System        Crypto Wallets and 2FA Extensions:        The stealer now searches for more information associated with the browser, such as crypto wallet and two-factor authentication (2FA) extensions that may have been installed.    The figure below shows the wallets and 2FA extensions that the stealer targets.    Figure 12\u00a0\u2013 Stealer Targeting Crypto Wallet And 2FA Extensions    In addition, the stealer can also steal browser history, login information, network cookies, and more from the system, as shown below.    Figure 13&nbsp;- Stealer Targeting Sensitive Browser Information        Command &amp; Control Communication        Finally, the stealer encrypts the data obtained from the infected system and sends it to the C&amp;C server, as shown below.    The figure below depicts the C&amp;C communication of the stealer.    Figure 14&nbsp;- C&amp;C Communication of the LummaC2 Stealer        Conclusion        LummaC2 behaves in a manner comparable to other stealer-type malware, which can take away both system and sensitive data from the victim's machine. These dangerous programs usually have the capacity to take information from web browsers and target Crypto wallets and 2FA extensions.    The additional information stored on web browsers, such as login credentials, PII, and financial information, can be further leveraged to conduct fraud activities as well.    Threat actors can use the stolen data to steal cryptocurrencies from the victim's accounts, or alternatively, they can sell this data to other threat actors for financial gain.    CRIL continuously monitors emerging threats and will continue to keep readers informed.    Our Recommendations        We have listed some essential cybersecurity best practices that create the first line of control against attackers. We recommend that our readers follow the best practices given below:&nbsp;    Safety Measures Needed to Prevent Malware Attacks         Refrain from opening untrusted links and email attachments without verifying their authenticity.&nbsp;    Use a reputed anti-virus and Internet security software package on your connected devices, including PC, laptop, and mobile.&nbsp;    Conduct regular backup practices and keep those backups offline or in a separate network.&nbsp;    Turn on the automatic software update feature on your computer, mobile, and other connected devices wherever possible and pragmatic.&nbsp;     Users Should Take the Following Steps After the Malware Attack&nbsp;         Detach infected devices on the same network.&nbsp;    Disconnect external storage devices if connected.&nbsp;    Inspect system logs for suspicious events.&nbsp;     Impact And Cruciality of Malware&nbsp;         Loss of valuable data.&nbsp;    Loss of the organization's reputation and integrity.&nbsp;    Loss of the organization's sensitive business information.&nbsp;    Disruption in organization operation.&nbsp;    Monetary loss.&nbsp;     MITRE ATT&amp;CK\u00ae Techniques <style>

    * :focus { outline: 0; }
        .scroll {
    height: 1vh;
    font-size: 1rem;
    display: flex;
    justify-content: center;
    align-items: center;
  }
    
    .text-marquee {
    
      position: relative;
      display: flex;
      align-items: center;
      overflow-x: hidden;
    
    }
     
    .text-single {
      position: relative;
      white-space: pre;
      padding: 0;
      margin: 0;
      will-change: transform;
    background: #000;
    }
     
    .text {
    
      padding: 0;
      display: inline-block;
      margin-right: 2.8rem;
     font-family: 'Poppins',sans-serif; 
     font-weight: 400; 
     font-size: 14px;
     color: #fff;
    }
    .values:focus,.values:active{
        border:none;
        outline: 0;
    }
    .values .text{
        margin-left: 2px;
        margin-right: 3px;
    }
    .keys .text{
        margin-right: 5px;
        margin-left: 2.8rem;
        font-weight: bold;
    }
  
    .text-single a:last-child .text{
         padding-right: 2.8rem!important; 
    }
    
    
      .text.js-text:hover, .text.js-text:active, .text.js-text:focus{
         outline: 0 none;
      -moz-outline: 0 none;
      }  
      
    </style>
<script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/jquery/3.6.0/jquery.min.js?ver<%=DateTime.Now.Ticks.ToString()%>" type="text/javascript"></script>
  
  
  
  <script src="https://unpkg.co/gsap@3/dist/gsap.min.js?ver<%=DateTime.Now.Ticks.ToString()%>" type="text/javascript"></script>
  
  
  
  <script src="https://unpkg.com/gsap@3/dist/Draggable.min.js?ver<%=DateTime.Now.Ticks.ToString()%>" type="text/javascript"></script>
  
  
  <script>
  document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function() {
      let loops = gsap.utils.toArray('.text-single').map((line, i) => {
          const links = line.querySelectorAll(".js-text"),
              tl = horizontalLoop(links, {
                  repeat: -1,
                  speed: 1 + i * 0.5,
                  draggable: true,
                  reversed: false,
                  paddingRight: parseFloat(gsap.getProperty(links[0], "marginRight", "px"))
              });
          links.forEach(link => {
              link.addEventListener("mouseenter", () => gsap.to(tl, {timeScale: 0, overwrite: true}));
              link.addEventListener("mouseleave", () => gsap.to(tl, {timeScale: i ? -1 : 1, overwrite: true}));
          });
      });
  
      let currentScroll = 0;
      let scrollDirection = 1;
  
      window.addEventListener("scroll", () => {
          let direction = (window.pageYOffset > currentScroll) ? 1 : -1;
          if (direction !== scrollDirection) {
              loops.forEach(tl => gsap.to(tl, {timeScale: direction, overwrite: true}));
              scrollDirection = direction;
          }
          currentScroll = window.pageYOffset;
      });
  
    function horizontalLoop(items, config) {
      items = gsap.utils.toArray(items);
      config = config || {};
      let tl = gsap.timeline({repeat: config.repeat, paused: config.paused, defaults: {ease: "none"}, onReverseComplete: () => tl.totalTime(tl.rawTime() + tl.duration() * 100)}),
          length = items.length,
          startX = items[0].offsetLeft,
          times = [],
          widths = [],
          xPercents = [],
          curIndex = 0,
          pixelsPerSecond = (config.speed || 1) * 100,
          snap = config.snap === false ? v => v : gsap.utils.snap(config.snap || 1), // some browsers shift by a pixel to accommodate flex layouts, so for example if width is 20% the first element's width might be 242px, and the next 243px, alternating back and forth. So we snap to 5 percentage points to make things look more natural
          populateWidths = () => items.forEach((el, i) => {
        widths[i] = parseFloat(gsap.getProperty(el, "width", "px"));
        xPercents[i] = snap(parseFloat(gsap.getProperty(el, "x", "px")) / widths[i] * 100 + gsap.getProperty(el, "xPercent"));
      }),
      getTotalWidth = () => items[length-1].offsetLeft + xPercents[length-1] / 100 * widths[length-1] - startX + items[length-1].offsetWidth * gsap.getProperty(items[length-1], "scaleX") + (parseFloat(config.paddingRight) || 0),
        totalWidth, curX, distanceToStart, distanceToLoop, item, i;
      populateWidths();
    gsap.set(items, { // convert "x" to "xPercent" to make things responsive, and populate the widths/xPercents Arrays to make lookups faster.
          xPercent: i => xPercents[i]
      });
      gsap.set(items, {x: 0});
      totalWidth = getTotalWidth();
      for (i = 0; i < length; i++) {
          item = items[i];
          curX = xPercents[i] / 100 * widths[i];
          distanceToStart = item.offsetLeft + curX - startX;
          distanceToLoop = distanceToStart + widths[i] * gsap.getProperty(item, "scaleX");
          tl.to(item, {xPercent: snap((curX - distanceToLoop) / widths[i] * 100), duration: distanceToLoop / pixelsPerSecond}, 0)
            .fromTo(item, {xPercent: snap((curX - distanceToLoop + totalWidth) / widths[i] * 100)}, {xPercent: xPercents[i], duration: (curX - distanceToLoop + totalWidth - curX) / pixelsPerSecond, immediateRender: false}, distanceToLoop / pixelsPerSecond)
            .add("label" + i, distanceToStart / pixelsPerSecond);
          times[i] = distanceToStart / pixelsPerSecond;
      }
      function toIndex(index, vars) {
          vars = vars || {};
          (Math.abs(index - curIndex) > length / 2) && (index += index > curIndex ? -length : length); // always go in the shortest direction
          let newIndex = gsap.utils.wrap(0, length, index),
              time = times[newIndex];
          if (time > tl.time() !== index > curIndex) { // if we're wrapping the timeline's playhead, make the proper adjustments
              vars.modifiers = {time: gsap.utils.wrap(0, tl.duration())};
              time += tl.duration() * (index > curIndex ? 1 : -1);
          }
          curIndex = newIndex;
          vars.overwrite = true;
          return tl.tweenTo(time, vars);
      }
      tl.next = vars => toIndex(curIndex+1, vars);
      tl.previous = vars => toIndex(curIndex-1, vars);
      tl.current = () => curIndex;
      tl.toIndex = (index, vars) => toIndex(index, vars);
    tl.updateIndex = () => curIndex = Math.round(tl.progress() * (items.length - 1));
      tl.times = times;
    tl.progress(1, true).progress(0, true); // pre-render for performance
    if (config.reversed) {
      tl.vars.onReverseComplete();
      tl.reverse();
    }
    if (config.draggable && typeof(Draggable) === "function") {
      let proxy = document.createElement("div"),
          wrap = gsap.utils.wrap(0, 1),
          ratio, startProgress, draggable, dragSnap, roundFactor,
          align = () => tl.progress(wrap(startProgress + (draggable.startX - draggable.x) * ratio)),
          syncIndex = () => tl.updateIndex();
      typeof(InertiaPlugin) === "undefined" && console.warn("InertiaPlugin required for momentum-based scrolling and snapping. https://greensock.com/club");
      draggable = Draggable.create(proxy, {
        trigger: items[0].parentNode,
        type: "x",
        onPress() {
          startProgress = tl.progress();
          tl.progress(0);
          populateWidths();
          totalWidth = getTotalWidth();
          ratio = 1 / totalWidth;
          dragSnap = totalWidth / items.length;
          roundFactor = Math.pow(10, ((dragSnap + "").split(".")[1] || "").length);
          tl.progress(startProgress);
        },
        onDrag: align,
        onThrowUpdate: align,
        inertia: true,
        snap: value => {
          let n = Math.round(parseFloat(value) / dragSnap) * dragSnap * roundFactor;
          return (n - n % 1) / roundFactor;
        },
        onRelease: syncIndex,
        onThrowComplete: () => gsap.set(proxy, {x: 0}) && syncIndex()
      })[0];
    }
    
      return tl;
  }
  });
  </script>

				</div>

				<div class="elementor-widget-container">
					<h1 class="elementor-heading-title elementor-size-default">LummaC2 Stealer: A Potent Threat to Crypto Users</h1>				</div>
				</div>
				<div class="elementor-element elementor-element-1fcc1d6c elementor-widget elementor-widget-theme-post-excerpt" data-id="1fcc1d6c" data-element_type="widget" data-widget_type="theme-post-excerpt.default">
				<div class="elementor-widget-container">
					CRIL analyzes the latest version of LummaC2 Stealer , targeting crypto users via stealing their crypto wallet and 2FA extensions.				</div>
				</div>
				<div class="elementor-element elementor-element-2907e1e2 blog_content elementor-widget elementor-widget-theme-post-content" data-id="2907e1e2" data-element_type="widget" data-widget_type="theme-post-content.default">
				<div class="elementor-widget-container">
					
<h2 class="wp-block-heading">New Stealer Targeting Crypto Wallets and 2FA Extensions of Various Browsers</h2>



<p></p>



<p>During a threat-hunting exercise, Cyble Research and Intelligence Labs (CRIL) discovered a post on the cybercrime forum about an information stealer targeting both Chromium and Mozilla-based browsers. This stealer was named LummaC2 Stealer, which targets crypto wallets, extensions, and two-factor authentication (2FA) and steals sensitive information from the victim&#8217;s machine.</p>



<p>The figure below shows the dark web post by the Threat Actors.</p><!-- This site is converting visitors into subscribers and customers with OptinMonster - https://optinmonster.com :: Campaign Title: Request demo blog -->

<p></p>



<p>The post also mentioned the link to LummaC2 Stealer&#8217;s seller website, which is written in Russian. The website also offers various purchasing options for potential <a class="wpil_keyword_link" href="https://cyble.com/knowledge-hub/cyber-threat-actor-and-types/" target="_blank" rel="noopener" title="Threat Actors" data-wpil-keyword-link="linked" data-wpil-monitor-id="1716">Threat Actors</a>(TAs), with prices ranging from $250 to $20000 depending on the plan.</p>



<p>The image below shows the website where the stealer is available for sale.</p>

<p></p>



<p>In addition, Threat Actors (TAs) behind the LummaC2 Stealer have created two Telegram channels in Russian: one for sharing information about the stealer and one for reporting bugs in the <a class="wpil_keyword_link" href="https://cyble.com/knowledge-hub/what-is-malware/" title="malware" data-wpil-keyword-link="linked" data-wpil-monitor-id="491" target="_blank">malware</a>.</p>

<p></p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="h-technical-details">Technical Details</h2>



<p></p>



<p>The LummaC2 Stealer is a 32-bit GUI type executable with sha256 d932ee10f02ea5bb60ed867d9687a906f1b8472f01fc5543b06f9ab22059b264.</p>



<p>The figure below shows the additional file details of the LummaC2 stealer executable.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image aligncenter size-full"><img data-recalc-dims="1" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="722" height="433" data-attachment-id="15067" data-permalink="https://cyble.com/blog/lummac2-stealer-a-potent-threat-to-crypto-users/figure-6-file-details-for-lummac2-stealer/" data-orig-file="https://i0.wp.com/cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/01/Figure-6-File-Details-for-LummaC2-Stealer.png?fit=722%2C433&amp;ssl=1" data-orig-size="722,433" data-comments-opened="0" data-image-meta="{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}" data-image-title="Figure-6-File-Details-for-LummaC2-Stealer" data-image-description="" data-image-caption="" data-medium-file="https://i0.wp.com/cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/01/Figure-6-File-Details-for-LummaC2-Stealer.png?fit=300%2C180&amp;ssl=1" data-large-file="https://i0.wp.com/cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/01/Figure-6-File-Details-for-LummaC2-Stealer.png?fit=722%2C433&amp;ssl=1" src="https://i0.wp.com/cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/01/Figure-6-File-Details-for-LummaC2-Stealer.png?resize=722%2C433&#038;ssl=1" alt="LummaC2 Stealer" class="wp-image-15067" title="LummaC2 Stealer: A Potent Threat to Crypto Users 20" srcset="https://i0.wp.com/cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/01/Figure-6-File-Details-for-LummaC2-Stealer.png?w=722&amp;ssl=1 722w, https://i0.wp.com/cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/01/Figure-6-File-Details-for-LummaC2-Stealer.png?resize=300%2C180&amp;ssl=1 300w" sizes="(max-width: 722px) 100vw, 722px" /><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">Figure 6 &#8211; File Details of LummaC2 Stealer</figcaption></figure>



<p></p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="h-detection-evasion">Detection Evasion:</h2>



<p></p>



<p>The stealer has many Obfuscated strings that are being covered by a random string, &#8220;edx765&#8221;, to evade detection. Upon execution, the stealer passes the obfuscated string to a function that strips the random string and delivers the original string.</p>



<p>The figure below shows the routine for string manipulation.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image aligncenter size-full"><img data-recalc-dims="1" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="783" height="299" data-attachment-id="15068" data-permalink="https://cyble.com/blog/lummac2-stealer-a-potent-threat-to-crypto-users/figure-7-assembly-code-to-replace-the-edx765-string/" data-orig-file="https://i0.wp.com/cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/01/Figure-7-Assembly-Code-to-Replace-the-edx765-String.png?fit=783%2C299&amp;ssl=1" data-orig-size="783,299" data-comments-opened="0" data-image-meta="{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}" data-image-title="Figure-7-Assembly-Code-to-Replace-the-edx765-String" data-image-description="" data-image-caption="" class="wp-element-caption">Figure 7 &#8211; Assembly Code to Replace the edx765 String</figcaption></figure>



<p></p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="h-collects-system-information">Collects System Information:</h2>



<p></p>



<p>After getting the required strings, the malware resolves the APIs. It starts extracting multiple pieces of information from the system, including LummaC2 Build, Lumma ID, Hardware ID, Screen Resolution, System Language, CPU Name, and Physical Memory. The malware stores this information in the memory under the name <em>system.txt</em>.</p>



<p>The below figure shows the code snippet of malware for collecting system information.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image aligncenter size-full"><img data-recalc-dims="1" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="697" height="517" data-attachment-id="15070" data-permalink="https://cyble.com/blog/lummac2-stealer-a-potent-threat-to-crypto-users/figure-8-system-information-extracted-by-the-stealer/" data-orig-file="https://i0.wp.com/cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/01/Figure-8-System-Information-Extracted-by-the-Stealer.png?fit=697%2C517&amp;ssl=1" data-orig-size="697,517" data-comments-opened="0" data-image-meta="{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}" data-image-title="Figure-8-System-Information-Extracted-by-the-Stealer" data-image-description="" data-image-caption="" data-medium-file="https://i0.wp.com/cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/01/Figure-8-System-Information-Extracted-by-the-Stealer.png?fit=300%2C223&amp;ssl=1" data-large-file="https://i0.wp.com/cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/01/Figure-8-System-Information-Extracted-by-the-Stealer.png?fit=697%2C517&amp;ssl=1" src="https://i0.wp.com/cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/01/Figure-8-System-Information-Extracted-by-the-Stealer.png?resize=697%2C517&#038;ssl=1" alt="LummaC2 Stealer" class="wp-image-15070" title="LummaC2 Stealer: A Potent Threat to Crypto Users 22" srcset="https://i0.wp.com/cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/01/Figure-8-System-Information-Extracted-by-the-Stealer.png?w=697&amp;ssl=1 697w, https://i0.wp.com/cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/01/Figure-8-System-Information-Extracted-by-the-Stealer.png?resize=300%2C223&amp;ssl=1 300w" sizes="(max-width: 697px) 100vw, 697px" /><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">Figure 8&nbsp;&#8211; System Information Extracted by the Stealer</figcaption></figure>



<p></p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="h-file-grabber">File Grabber:</h2>



<p></p>



<p>The stealer now enumerates the <em>%userProfile%</em> directory and grabs .txt files from the Victims machine. These grabbed files are stored in the memory under the name &#8220;<em>Important Files/Profile</em>&#8221; for exfiltration.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="h-wallets">Wallets:</h2>



<p></p>



<p>The stealer also targets crypto wallets such as Binance, Electrum, and Ethereum and collects sensitive information from the victim&#8217;s machine. The below figure shows the code snippet of stealers targeting crypto wallets.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image aligncenter size-full"><img data-recalc-dims="1" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="623" height="268" data-attachment-id="15071" data-permalink="https://cyble.com/blog/lummac2-stealer-a-potent-threat-to-crypto-users/figure-9-the-stealer-targeting-wallets/" data-orig-file="https://i0.wp.com/cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/01/Figure-9-The-Stealer-Targeting-Wallets.png?fit=623%2C268&amp;ssl=1" data-orig-size="623,268" data-comments-opened="0" data-image-meta="{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}" data-image-title="Figure-9-The-Stealer-Targeting-Wallets" data-image-description="" data-image-caption="" data-medium-file="https://i0.wp.com/cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/01/Figure-9-The-Stealer-Targeting-Wallets.png?fit=300%2C129&amp;ssl=1" data-large-file="https://i0.wp.com/cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/01/Figure-9-The-Stealer-Targeting-Wallets.png?fit=623%2C268&amp;ssl=1" src="https://i0.wp.com/cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/01/Figure-9-The-Stealer-Targeting-Wallets.png?resize=623%2C268&#038;ssl=1" alt="LummaC2 Stealer" class="wp-image-15071" title="LummaC2 Stealer: A Potent Threat to Crypto Users 23" srcset="https://i0.wp.com/cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/01/Figure-9-The-Stealer-Targeting-Wallets.png?w=623&amp;ssl=1 623w, https://i0.wp.com/cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/01/Figure-9-The-Stealer-Targeting-Wallets.png?resize=300%2C129&amp;ssl=1 300w" sizes="(max-width: 623px) 100vw, 623px" /><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">Figure 9&nbsp;&#8211; The Stealer Targeting Wallets</figcaption></figure>



<p></p>



<p>After collecting the victim&#8217;s wallet and system details, the stealer sends this information to its C&amp;C server, as shown below.</p>

<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="h-browsers">Browsers:</h2>



<p></p>



<p>After sending the stolen information, the stealer checks for the following browsers installed on the system: Chrome, Chromium, Edge, Kometa, Vivaldi, Brave, Opera Stable, Opera GX Stable, Opera Neon, and Mozilla Firefox and steals sensitive information from the browsers.</p>

<p>Finally, the stealer encrypts the data obtained from the infected system and sends it to the C&amp;C server, as shown below.</p>

<p></p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="h-conclusion">Conclusion</h2>



<p></p>



<p>LummaC2 behaves in a manner comparable to other stealer-type malware, which can take away both system and sensitive data from the victim&#8217;s machine. These dangerous programs usually have the capacity to take information from web browsers and target Crypto wallets and 2FA extensions.</p>



<p>The additional information stored on web browsers, such as login credentials, PII, and financial information, can be further leveraged to conduct fraud activities as well.</p>



<p>Threat actors can use the stolen data to steal cryptocurrencies from the victim&#8217;s accounts, or alternatively, they can sell this data to other threat actors for financial gain.</p>



<p>CRIL continuously monitors emerging threats and will continue to keep readers informed.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="h-our-recommendations">Our Recommendations</h2>



<p></p>



<p>We have listed some essential <a class="wpil_keyword_link" href="https://cyble.com/knowledge-hub/cybersecurity/" target="_blank" rel="noopener" title="cybersecurity" data-wpil-keyword-link="linked" data-wpil-monitor-id="1715">cybersecurity</a> best practices that create the first line of control against attackers. We recommend that our readers follow the best practices given below:&nbsp;</p>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading">Safety Measures Needed to Prevent Malware Attacks</h3>



<p></p>



<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li>Refrain from opening untrusted links and email attachments without verifying their authenticity.&nbsp;</li>



<li>Use a reputed anti-virus and Internet security software package on your connected devices, including PC, laptop, and mobile.&nbsp;</li>



<li>Conduct regular backup practices and keep those backups offline or in a separate network.&nbsp;</li>



<li>Turn on the automatic software update feature on your computer, mobile, and other connected devices wherever possible and pragmatic.&nbsp;</li>
</ul>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading">Users Should Take the Following Steps After the Malware Attack&nbsp;</h3>



<p></p>



<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li>Detach infected devices on the same network.&nbsp;</li>



<li>Disconnect external storage devices if connected.&nbsp;</li>



<li>Inspect system logs for suspicious events.&nbsp;</li>
</ul>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading">Impact And Cruciality of Malware&nbsp;</h3>



<p></p>



<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li>Loss of valuable data.&nbsp;</li>



<li>Loss of the organization&#8217;s reputation and integrity.&nbsp;</li>



<li>Loss of the organization&#8217;s sensitive business information.&nbsp;</li>



<li>Disruption in organization operation.&nbsp;</li>



<li>Monetary loss.&nbsp;</li>
</ul>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="h-mitre-att-ck-techniques">MITRE ATT&amp;CK® Techniques</h2>



<p></p>



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table><tbody><tr><td><strong>Tactic&nbsp;</strong></td><td><strong>Technique ID&nbsp;</strong></td><td><strong>Technique Name&nbsp;</strong></td></tr><tr><td><strong>Defense Evasion&nbsp;</strong></td><td><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1140/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">T1140</a><br><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">T1562</a></td><td>Deobfuscate/Decode Files or Information<br>Impair Defences</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Discovery&nbsp;</strong></td><td><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1082/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener nofollow">T1082</a>&nbsp;<br><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1083/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener nofollow">T1083</a>&nbsp;</td><td>System Information Discovery&nbsp;<br>File and Directory Discovery&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Collection</strong><strong></strong></td><td><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1119/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">T1119</a> <br><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1005/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">T1005</a></td><td>Automated Collection <br>Data from the Local System</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Command and&nbsp;Control&nbsp;</strong></td><td><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1071/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener nofollow">T1071</a>&nbsp;</td><td>Application Layer Protocol&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Exfiltration&nbsp;</strong></td><td><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1020/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener nofollow">T1020</a>&nbsp;</td><td>Automated Exfiltration&nbsp;</td></tr></tbody></table></figure>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="h-indicators-of-compromise-iocs">Indicators of Compromise (IoCs)</h2>



<p></p>



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table><tbody><tr><td><strong>Indicators</strong></td><td><strong>Indicator Type</strong></td><td><strong>Description</strong></td></tr><tr><td><strong>1995a54dba0e05d80903d3d210c1e3da</strong> <br><strong>c43316ddcb51e143ab53f996587c23ea4985f6ea</strong> <br><strong>277d7f450268aeb4e7fe942f70a9df63aa429d703e9400370f0621a438e918bf</strong></td><td>MD5 <br>SHA1 <br>SHA256</td><td>LummaC2 Binary</td></tr><tr><td><strong>a09daf5791d8fd4b5843cd38ae37cf97</strong> <br><strong>2c11592f527a35c3dac75139e870dd062b12dfe1</strong> <br><strong>60247d4ddd08204818b60ade4bfc32d6c31756c574a5fe2cd521381385a0f868</strong></td><td>MD5 <br>SHA1 <br>SHA256</td><td>LummaC2 Binary</td></tr><tr><td><strong>5aac51312dfd99bf4e88be482f734c79</strong> <br><strong>9ac88b93fee8f888cabc3d0c9d81507c6dad7498</strong> <br><strong>9b742a890aff9c7a2b54b620fe5e1fcfa553648695d79c892564de09b850c92b</strong></td><td>MD5 <br>SHA1 <br>SHA256</td><td>LummaC2 Binary</td></tr><tr><td><strong>c9c0e32e00d084653db0b37a239e9a34</strong> <br><strong>b97965e4a793ec0fa10abc86d0c6be5718716d8a</strong> <strong>d932ee10f02ea5bb60ed867d9687a906f1b8472f01fc5543b06f9ab22059b264</strong></td><td>MD5 <br>SHA1 <br>SHA256</td><td>LummaC2 Binary</td></tr><tr><td>195[.]123[.]226[.]91</td><td>IP</td><td>LummaC2 C&amp;C</td></tr><tr><td>144[.]76[.]173[.]247</td><td>IP</td><td>LummaC2 C&amp;C</td></tr></tbody></table></figure>

<script>
   let autoHideTimeout;

document.addEventListener('scroll', function() {
    var scrollPosition = window.scrollY || document.documentElement.scrollTop;
    var documentHeight = document.documentElement.scrollHeight - document.documentElement.clientHeight;

    // Calculate scroll percentage
    var scrollPercentage = (scrollPosition / documentHeight) * 100;

    // Check if the screen width is greater than 768px (for non-mobile devices)
    if (window.innerWidth > 768) {
        // Only activate the slider when scroll is between 60% and 100%
        if (scrollPercentage >= 60 && scrollPercentage <= 100) {
            // Show the slider by sliding it in
            document.getElementById('rightSlider').classList.add('active');

            // Clear any previous auto-hide timer
            clearTimeout(autoHideTimeout);

            // Set a 5-second timer to auto-slide the slider back out
            autoHideTimeout = setTimeout(function() {
                document.getElementById('rightSlider').classList.remove('active');
            }, 5000); // 5000 milliseconds = 5 seconds
        } else {
            // If not within 60% - 100% range, hide the slider
            document.getElementById('rightSlider').classList.remove('active');
        }
    }
});

document.getElementById('rightSlider').addEventListener('mouseover', function() {
    // On mouseover, keep the slider active and clear the auto-hide timer
    clearTimeout(autoHideTimeout);
    this.classList.add('active');
});

document.getElementById('rightSlider').addEventListener('mouseleave', function() {
    // On mouse leave, start the auto-hide timer again for 5 seconds
    clearTimeout(autoHideTimeout);
    autoHideTimeout = setTimeout(function() {
        document.getElementById('rightSlider').classList.remove('active');
    }, 5000); // 5000 milliseconds = 5 seconds
});

</script>				</div>

					<script type='text/javascript'>
				const lazyloadRunObserver = () => {
					const lazyloadBackgrounds = document.querySelectorAll( `.e-con.e-parent:not(.e-lazyloaded)` );
					const lazyloadBackgroundObserver = new IntersectionObserver( ( entries ) => {
						entries.forEach( ( entry ) => {
							if ( entry.isIntersecting ) {
								let lazyloadBackground = entry.target;
								if( lazyloadBackground ) {
									lazyloadBackground.classList.add( 'e-lazyloaded' );
								}
								lazyloadBackgroundObserver.unobserve( entry.target );
							}
						});
					}, { rootMargin: '200px 0px 200px 0px' } );
					lazyloadBackgrounds.forEach( ( lazyloadBackground ) => {
						lazyloadBackgroundObserver.observe( lazyloadBackground );
					} );
				};
				const events = [
					'DOMContentLoaded',
					'elementor/lazyload/observe',
				];
				events.forEach( ( event ) => {
					document.addEventListener( event, lazyloadRunObserver );
				} );
			</script>
